EVI5

The immune function of the gene EVI5 (Ecotropic Viral Integration Site 5) is primarily linked to its roles in hematopoiesis, immune cell regulation, and its implications in cancer:

  1. Regulation of Hematopoietic Stem Cells:
    • EVI5 is involved in the regulation of hematopoietic stem cells (HSCs), influencing their proliferation and differentiation. This is crucial for maintaining a healthy immune system, as HSCs give rise to various immune cell types.
  2. Impact on Immune Cell Function:
    • EVI5 has been shown to play a role in the differentiation and function of specific immune cells, including T cells. Its expression can affect the development and activation of these cells, which are essential for adaptive immunity.
  3. Association with Cancer Immunology:
    • In the context of acute myeloid leukemia (AML), EVI5 is implicated in promoting an immunosuppressive tumor microenvironment. It can influence the expression of genes associated with immune evasion, potentially leading to poor outcomes in patients with EVI5-overexpressing tumors.
  4. Interaction with Cytokine Signaling:
    • EVI5 may interact with pathways involving cytokines such as interferon-gamma (IFN-γ), which is known to play a role in shaping immune responses and promoting an immunosuppressive environment in tumors. This interaction suggests that EVI5 could modulate the immune landscape within cancers.
  5. Potential for Therapeutic Targeting:
    • Given its role in both hematopoiesis and cancer immunology, EVI5 presents potential as a therapeutic target for enhancing anti-tumor immunity or improving outcomes in hematological malignancies.

In summary, EVI5 plays a significant role in regulating immune cell development and function, particularly within the context of hematopoiesis and cancer. Its influence on immune responses and tumor microenvironments highlights its importance in both normal immune function and disease processes.

IRX3

The immune function of the gene IRX3 (Iroquois Homeobox 3) is associated with its role in regulating hematopoiesis and influencing immune cell differentiation:

  1. Role in Hematopoiesis:
    • IRX3 is part of the Iroquois homeobox gene family, which plays critical roles in the development and differentiation of hematopoietic cells. It has been implicated in the regulation of hematopoietic progenitor cells, influencing their differentiation into various immune cell lineages.
  2. Influence on Lymphocyte Development:
    • Studies suggest that IRX3 may be involved in the development of lymphocytes, particularly B cells. Its expression patterns during hematopoiesis indicate a potential role in early lymphoid development, which is crucial for generating functional immune cells.
  3. Aberrant Expression in Hematologic Malignancies:
    • Dysregulation of IRX3 has been observed in various hematologic malignancies, including acute lymphoblastic leukemia (ALL). This aberrant expression can disrupt normal immune cell differentiation and contribute to the pathogenesis of these diseases.
  4. Transcriptional Regulation:
    • As a transcription factor, IRX3 can regulate the expression of genes involved in immune cell development and function. This regulatory capacity suggests that it plays a significant role in shaping the immune landscape during both normal development and pathological conditions.
  5. Potential Impact on Immune Responses:
    • By influencing the differentiation and function of immune cells, IRX3 may indirectly affect immune responses to infections and tumors. Its role in maintaining proper hematopoietic function underscores its importance in overall immune system health.

In summary, IRX3 plays a significant role in the regulation of hematopoiesis and lymphocyte development, with implications for immune function and responses. Its involvement in hematologic malignancies further highlights its importance in both normal and pathological immune processes.

RHOD

The immune function of the gene RHOD (Rho D) is primarily associated with its role in regulating the cytoskeleton and influencing immune cell behavior, particularly in the context of cell migration, activation, and signaling:

  1. Cytoskeletal Dynamics:
    • RHOD is a member of the Rho family of small GTPases, which are critical regulators of the cytoskeleton. By controlling actin filament organization, RHOD influences various cellular processes including cell shape, motility, and adhesion, all of which are essential for immune cell function.
  2. Regulation of Immune Cell Migration:
    • RHOD plays a significant role in the migration of immune cells to sites of infection or inflammation. Its activity can enhance the ability of immune cells to navigate through tissues, facilitating their recruitment to areas where they are needed to mount an immune response.
  3. Impact on T Cell Activation:
    • Studies indicate that RHOD may be involved in T cell activation processes. It can influence the formation of the immunological synapse, which is crucial for effective T cell signaling and activation upon encountering antigens.
  4. Role in Cytokine Secretion:
    • By regulating cytoskeletal rearrangements, RHOD may also impact the secretion of cytokines from immune cells. Proper cytokine release is essential for coordinating immune responses and communicating between different immune cell types.
  5. Involvement in Phagocytosis:
    • RHOD has been implicated in phagocytosis, the process by which immune cells engulf and digest pathogens. Its regulation of actin dynamics is vital for the formation of membrane extensions that surround and internalize pathogens.
  6. Potential Implications in Disease:
    • Dysregulation of RHOD function can lead to impaired immune responses, contributing to various diseases including autoimmune disorders and infections. Understanding its role could provide insights into therapeutic strategies aimed at enhancing immune function or correcting defects.

In summary, RHOD is an important regulator of cytoskeletal dynamics that influences various aspects of immune cell function, including migration, activation, cytokine secretion, and phagocytosis. Its role underscores the importance of cytoskeletal regulation in maintaining effective immune responses.

FOXJ1

The immune function of the gene FOXJ1 (Forkhead Box J1) is primarily associated with its role in regulating cilia formation and function, which has implications for immune responses, particularly in mucosal immunity and inflammation:

  1. Cilia Formation and Function:
    • FOXJ1 is a transcription factor that plays a critical role in the development of motile cilia. These cilia are essential for clearing mucus and pathogens from epithelial surfaces, particularly in the respiratory tract. Effective ciliary function is crucial for maintaining airway homeostasis and preventing infections.
  2. Mucosal Immunity:
    • By promoting cilia formation, FOXJ1 contributes to mucosal immunity. Ciliated epithelial cells help to trap and expel pathogens and debris, thus playing a protective role against respiratory infections. This function is vital for the innate immune response in the airways.
  3. Regulation of Inflammatory Responses:
    • FOXJ1 may also influence inflammatory responses in the lungs. The presence of functional cilia can modulate the local immune environment by affecting the recruitment and activity of immune cells, such as macrophages and neutrophils, which are involved in responding to infections.
  4. Role in Chronic Respiratory Diseases:
    • Dysregulation of FOXJ1 expression has been linked to chronic respiratory diseases, such as asthma and chronic obstructive pulmonary disease (COPD). In these conditions, impaired ciliary function can lead to increased mucus accumulation and inflammation, exacerbating disease symptoms.
  5. Potential Impact on Autoimmunity:
    • There is emerging evidence that FOXJ1 may play a role in autoimmune processes by influencing the behavior of immune cells at mucosal surfaces. Its involvement in regulating epithelial cell responses could affect how the immune system interacts with environmental antigens.
  6. Therapeutic Implications:
    • Understanding the role of FOXJ1 in ciliary function and mucosal immunity may have therapeutic implications for treating respiratory diseases and enhancing mucosal defenses against infections.

In summary, FOXJ1 is crucial for the formation and function of motile cilia, which are essential for mucosal immunity and maintaining airway health. Its role in regulating inflammatory responses underscores its importance in both protective immunity and the pathogenesis of respiratory diseases.

ADGRG1

The immune function of the gene ADGRG1 (Adhesion G Protein-Coupled Receptor G1), also known as GPR56, is primarily associated with its roles in immune cell regulation, particularly in the context of lymphocyte development and immune responses:

  1. Regulation of Lymphocyte Development:
    • ADGRG1 is expressed in various immune cells, including T cells and B cells. It plays a significant role in the development and differentiation of these lymphocytes, influencing their fate decisions during immune responses. Specifically, it has been implicated in B cell fate decisions, which are crucial for effective humoral immunity.
  2. Modulation of Immune Cell Activation:
    • ADGRG1 is involved in modulating the activation and function of immune cells. For example, its expression can affect T cell activation and the production of cytokines, thereby influencing the adaptive immune response. This modulation is essential for maintaining a balanced immune response and preventing excessive inflammation.
  3. Impact on Immune Surveillance:
    • The receptor has been shown to play a role in the surveillance functions of immune cells. By regulating the migration and adhesion of lymphocytes to tissues, ADGRG1 contributes to the ability of these cells to respond to infections and other immune challenges effectively.
  4. Involvement in Inflammation:
    • ADGRG1 has been linked to inflammatory processes. Its activation can influence the behavior of granulocytes (such as neutrophils), enhancing their antimicrobial activity and promoting the production of reactive oxygen species (ROS). This suggests that ADGRG1 plays a role in innate immunity by modulating the inflammatory response during infections.
  5. Potential Role in Autoimmunity:
    • Dysregulation of ADGRG1 expression or function may contribute to autoimmune conditions by affecting lymphocyte behavior and leading to inappropriate immune activation or tolerance breakdown.
  6. Therapeutic Implications:
    • Given its roles in regulating lymphocyte function and inflammation, ADGRG1 may represent a potential therapeutic target for modulating immune responses in various diseases, including autoimmune disorders and cancers.

In summary, ADGRG1 is an important regulator of immune cell development and function, influencing both adaptive and innate immune responses. Its involvement in lymphocyte differentiation, activation, and inflammatory processes underscores its significance in maintaining immune homeostasis and responding to pathological conditions.

SATB1

The immune function of the gene SATB1 (Special AT-rich Sequence-Binding Protein 1) is multifaceted, playing critical roles in T cell development, regulation, and immune responses:

  1. T Cell Development:
    • SATB1 is essential for normal T cell development in the thymus. It influences the differentiation of T cells by regulating the expression of genes involved in T cell maturation and function, particularly during the transition from double-positive to single-positive thymocytes.
  2. Regulation of T Cell Activation:
    • SATB1 is involved in the activation of cytotoxic T lymphocytes (CTLs). It helps coordinate the expression of genes necessary for CTL activation and effector functions, contributing to effective immune responses against tumors and infections.
  3. Influence on T Regulatory Cells:
    • SATB1 expression is downregulated in regulatory T cells (Tregs), suggesting that it plays a role in maintaining the balance between effector T cells and Tregs. This balance is crucial for preventing excessive immune responses and maintaining self-tolerance.
  4. Tumor Immunology:
    • SATB1 has been implicated in tumor immunology, where its expression can affect the behavior of immune cells within the tumor microenvironment. Increased SATB1 expression in tumor-infiltrating Tregs and dendritic cells can lead to an immunosuppressive phenotype, promoting tumor growth and progression.
  5. Prevention of T Cell Exhaustion:
    • SATB1 has been shown to help avoid T cell exhaustion, a state where T cells lose their ability to respond effectively to antigens. Its presence is associated with enhanced anti-tumor immunity, as it maintains a more functional state in activated T cells.
  6. Role in Inflammation:
    • By modulating the expression of various cytokines and chemokines, SATB1 can influence inflammatory responses. Its regulation of immune cell interactions within inflamed tissues underscores its importance in both protective immunity and pathological inflammation.
  7. Epigenetic Regulation:
    • SATB1 acts as an epigenetic regulator, shaping the chromatin landscape of immune cells. This regulation allows for the coordinated expression of multiple genes involved in immune function, facilitating rapid responses during immune challenges.

In summary, SATB1 is a crucial regulator of immune function, influencing T cell development, activation, and differentiation while also playing significant roles in tumor immunology and inflammatory responses. Its ability to modulate gene expression patterns makes it a key player in maintaining immune homeostasis and responding effectively to pathogens and tumors.

HLA-DPB1

The immune function of the gene HLA-DPB1 (Major Histocompatibility Complex, Class II, DP Beta 1) is crucial for the adaptive immune response, particularly in the context of antigen presentation:

  1. Antigen Presentation:
    • HLA-DPB1 is a part of the human leukocyte antigen (HLA) complex and encodes a protein that forms a heterodimer with another protein called HLA-DPA1. This complex is expressed on the surface of antigen-presenting cells (APCs), such as B cells, dendritic cells, and macrophages. HLA-DPB1 presents peptides derived from extracellular proteins to CD4+ T cells, facilitating their activation and proliferation in response to foreign antigens, such as those from pathogens or tumors [2][3].
  2. Role in Immune Responses:
    • The binding of peptide fragments to HLA-DPB1 allows the immune system to distinguish between self and non-self proteins. This is critical for initiating appropriate immune responses against infections and for activating helper T cells, which in turn stimulate B cells to produce antibodies [2][3][4].
  3. Genetic Variability and Immune Response:
    • HLA-DPB1 exhibits significant polymorphism, meaning there are many different alleles that can affect how well certain peptides bind to the molecule. This variability can influence individual immune responses to infections and vaccines. For example, specific alleles of HLA-DPB1 have been associated with varying levels of antibody responses to vaccines like the Japanese encephalitis vaccine [4].
  4. Association with Autoimmune Diseases:
    • Variants of the HLA-DPB1 gene have been linked to autoimmune conditions such as granulomatosis with polyangiitis and chronic beryllium disease. These associations suggest that certain alleles may predispose individuals to inappropriate immune responses against their own tissues [2][3].
  5. Tumor Immunology:
    • In cancer contexts, HLA-DPB1 expression is associated with tumor-infiltrating lymphocytes (TILs). High levels of HLA-DPB1 may correlate with increased immune infiltration by CD8+ T cells and other immune cell types, which can enhance anti-tumor immunity [1][4].

In summary, HLA-DPB1 plays a vital role in the immune system by facilitating the presentation of antigens to T cells, thereby initiating and regulating adaptive immune responses. Its genetic variability can influence individual susceptibility to infections, vaccine responses, and autoimmune diseases, highlighting its importance in immunology.

SIPA1L3

The immune function of the gene SIPA1L3 (Signal-Induced Proliferation-Associated 1-Like 3) is primarily linked to its role in regulating immune cell trafficking and signaling, particularly through its involvement with the Rap1 GTPase pathway:

  1. Regulation of Lymphocyte Trafficking:
    • SIPA1L3 is known to act as a GTPase-activating protein (GAP) for Rap1, a small GTPase that plays a critical role in the regulation of integrins and cell adhesion. By inactivating Rap1, SIPA1L3 helps modulate the adhesion and migration of lymphocytes, which is essential for their proper trafficking to sites of inflammation or infection [2].
  2. Impact on T Cell Function:
    • In T cells, SIPA1L3 deficiency has been shown to lead to increased activation of Rap1, resulting in enhanced adhesion and altered migration patterns. This can affect how T cells respond to chemokines and navigate through tissues, which is crucial for effective immune surveillance and response [2].
  3. Influence on Immune Responses:
    • The regulation of lymphocyte trafficking by SIPA1L3 is vital for maintaining immune homeostasis. Proper function of this gene ensures that T cells can effectively enter lymph nodes and exit back into circulation, which is necessary for mounting appropriate immune responses [2].
  4. Role in Autoimmunity:
    • Mice deficient in SIPA1L3 have been observed to develop late-onset autoimmune diseases, suggesting that proper regulation of this gene is important for preventing inappropriate immune activation and maintaining tolerance [2][4].
  5. Potential Implications in Cancer:
    • Alterations in SIPA1L3 expression may also have implications in cancer biology, particularly regarding how tumor-infiltrating lymphocytes interact with the tumor microenvironment. Dysregulated trafficking could affect the ability of immune cells to target tumors effectively [4].
  6. Interplay with Other Immune Mechanisms:
    • The interaction between SIPA1L3 and other signaling pathways highlights its role as a critical regulator within the broader context of immune cell dynamics. For example, its effects on integrin-mediated adhesion can influence how immune cells respond to various stimuli during an immune challenge [2].

In summary, SIPA1L3 plays a significant role in regulating lymphocyte trafficking and signaling through its action on the Rap1 pathway. Its function is crucial for maintaining effective immune responses and preventing autoimmune conditions, making it an important player in the immune system’s ability to respond to pathogens and maintain homeostasis.

PDLIM5

The immune function of the gene PDLIM5 (PDZ and LIM Domain 5) is primarily associated with its role in regulating immune cell signaling and inflammatory responses:

  1. Regulation of NF-κB Signaling:
    • PDLIM5 is involved in the modulation of the NF-κB signaling pathway, which is critical for the activation of immune responses. By interacting with components of this pathway, PDLIM5 can influence the transcription of pro-inflammatory cytokines and chemokines, thereby affecting the overall inflammatory response in immune cells.
  2. Impact on Cytokine Production:
    • Similar to other members of the PDZ-LIM protein family, PDLIM5 may act as a negative regulator of NF-κB-mediated signaling. This regulation helps prevent excessive inflammation, which can lead to tissue damage and chronic inflammatory diseases. Increased expression of PDLIM5 has been associated with reduced production of pro-inflammatory cytokines, indicating its role in controlling inflammatory responses.
  3. Role in Immune Cell Function:
    • PDLIM5 is expressed in various immune cells, including T cells and dendritic cells. Its presence in these cells suggests it may play a role in their activation, differentiation, and migration, which are essential for effective immune surveillance and response.
  4. Potential Implications in Autoimmunity and Cancer:
    • Dysregulation of PDLIM5 may contribute to autoimmune conditions by failing to adequately control inflammatory responses. In cancer, alterations in PDLIM5 expression could influence tumor progression by modulating the immune microenvironment, potentially affecting how tumors evade immune detection.
  5. Interplay with Other Proteins:
    • PDLIM5 interacts with various signaling molecules and cytoskeletal components, facilitating the formation of protein complexes that regulate cellular responses to external stimuli. This interaction is crucial for maintaining proper immune cell function and communication.

In summary, PDLIM5 plays a significant role in regulating immune responses through its involvement in NF-κB signaling and cytokine production. Its functions in immune cell activation and migration underscore its importance in maintaining immune homeostasis and responding to pathological conditions. Further research into PDLIM5 could provide insights into its potential as a therapeutic target for inflammatory diseases and cancer.

BCL2L14

The immune function of the gene BCL2L14 (BCL2-like 14) is primarily associated with its role in regulating apoptosis and influencing immune cell survival and function:

  1. Regulation of Apoptosis:
    • BCL2L14 is part of the Bcl-2 family of proteins, which are critical regulators of the apoptotic pathway. Specifically, BCL2L14 functions as a pro-apoptotic protein, promoting programmed cell death in certain contexts. This regulation is essential for maintaining immune homeostasis by controlling the lifespan of immune cells, such as T and B lymphocytes.
  2. Influence on Lymphocyte Development:
    • By modulating apoptosis, BCL2L14 plays a role in lymphocyte development. Proper regulation of cell death during immune cell maturation ensures that only functional and appropriately activated cells survive, which is crucial for effective immune responses.
  3. Impact on Immune Responses:
    • The expression levels of BCL2L14 can influence the activation and proliferation of immune cells. For instance, in activated T cells, increased levels of BCL2L14 can promote apoptosis, thereby regulating the expansion of T cell populations after an immune response has been mounted.
  4. Role in Autoimmunity:
    • Dysregulation of BCL2L14 may contribute to autoimmune diseases by affecting the survival and activation of autoreactive lymphocytes. If apoptotic pathways are not properly regulated, this can lead to an accumulation of potentially harmful immune cells that attack self-tissues.
  5. Cancer Immunology:
    • In cancer contexts, BCL2L14 may influence tumor immunity by regulating the survival of tumor-infiltrating lymphocytes (TILs). The balance between pro-apoptotic and anti-apoptotic signals can affect how well these immune cells can persist within the tumor microenvironment and exert their anti-tumor effects.
  6. Interactions with Other Proteins:
    • BCL2L14 interacts with other members of the Bcl-2 family to modulate apoptotic signaling pathways. These interactions are critical for determining whether a cell will undergo apoptosis or survive under various conditions, including stress or infection.

In summary, BCL2L14 plays a significant role in regulating apoptosis within the immune system, influencing lymphocyte development, activation, and survival. Its functions are crucial for maintaining immune homeostasis and preventing autoimmune responses while also impacting tumor immunity. Understanding its role could provide insights into therapeutic strategies for autoimmune diseases and cancer immunotherapy.

UBE2E2

The immune function of the gene UBE2E2 (Ubiquitin Conjugating Enzyme E2 E2) is primarily associated with its role in the ubiquitination process, which is critical for regulating various immune responses:

  1. Ubiquitination and Immune Signaling:
    • UBE2E2 is involved in the ubiquitination of proteins, a post-translational modification that can alter protein stability, localization, and activity. This process is essential for regulating immune signaling pathways, including those involved in the activation of immune cells and the modulation of inflammatory responses.
  2. Regulation of NF-κB Pathway:
    • UBE2E2 has been implicated in the regulation of the NF-κB signaling pathway, which plays a crucial role in mediating immune responses and inflammation. By facilitating the ubiquitination of specific substrates, UBE2E2 can influence NF-κB activation and its downstream effects on cytokine production and immune cell activation.
  3. Impact on Cytokine Production:
    • Through its role in ubiquitination, UBE2E2 can affect the production of pro-inflammatory cytokines. This regulation is vital for coordinating immune responses to infections and other immune challenges.
  4. Influence on Immune Cell Survival and Proliferation:
    • UBE2E2 may also play a role in regulating the survival and proliferation of immune cells. By modulating the degradation of proteins involved in cell cycle regulation and apoptosis, it contributes to maintaining appropriate levels of immune cell populations during an immune response.
  5. Potential Role in Autoimmunity and Cancer:
    • Dysregulation of UBE2E2 expression or function can lead to altered immune responses, contributing to autoimmune diseases or impacting tumor immunity. For example, improper regulation of cytokine signaling pathways can result in chronic inflammation or ineffective anti-tumor immunity.
  6. Interplay with Other Ubiquitin Ligases:
    • UBE2E2 often works in conjunction with E3 ubiquitin ligases to target specific proteins for ubiquitination. This collaboration is crucial for fine-tuning immune signaling pathways and ensuring that immune responses are appropriately activated or suppressed.

In summary, UBE2E2 plays a significant role in regulating immune functions through its involvement in ubiquitination processes that modulate signaling pathways, cytokine production, and immune cell dynamics. Its importance in maintaining immune homeostasis highlights its potential as a target for therapeutic interventions in autoimmune diseases and cancer.

LMO4

The immune function of the gene LMO4 (LIM Domain Only 4) is primarily associated with its role in enhancing CD8+ T cell responses and promoting T cell memory formation:

  1. Enhancement of CD8+ T Cell Stemness:
    • LMO4 has been shown to boost the stem-like properties of CD8+ T cells, which are crucial for long-term immunity. By promoting the generation and maintenance of stem-like memory T cells, LMO4 enhances the ability of these cells to respond to subsequent infections or tumor challenges.
  2. Modulation of Cytokine Signaling:
    • LMO4 interacts with signaling pathways, notably potentiating STAT3 signaling in response to interleukin-21 (IL-21). This interaction promotes the expression of genes important for memory T cell development and function, thereby enhancing the overall immune response.
  3. Promotion of Antitumor Immunity:
    • In preclinical models, overexpression of LMO4 in CD8+ T cells has been linked to improved antitumor immunity. This results in increased tumor regression and enhanced persistence of T cells in the tumor microenvironment, suggesting that LMO4 can be a valuable target for improving cancer immunotherapies.
  4. Increased Polyfunctionality:
    • CD8+ T cells overexpressing LMO4 exhibit increased polyfunctional capabilities, meaning they can produce multiple cytokines simultaneously. This polyfunctionality is critical for effective immune responses, as it enhances the ability of T cells to combat infections and tumors.
  5. Impact on Memory T Cell Formation:
    • LMO4 helps maintain a balance between effector and memory T cell populations by curbing terminal differentiation. This ensures that a reservoir of memory T cells is available for rapid response upon re-exposure to antigens.
  6. Potential Therapeutic Applications:
    • Given its role in enhancing T cell function and memory formation, LMO4 could be targeted in therapeutic strategies aimed at improving vaccine efficacy or developing more effective adoptive T cell therapies for cancer treatment.

In summary, LMO4 plays a significant role in regulating CD8+ T cell immunity by enhancing their stem-like properties, modulating cytokine signaling, promoting antitumor responses, and increasing the formation of polyfunctional memory T cells. Its functions make it a promising candidate for applications in immunotherapy and vaccine development.

PPP1R14A

The immune function of the gene PPP1R14A (Protein Phosphatase 1 Regulatory Inhibitor Subunit 14A) is primarily associated with its regulatory role in immune cell signaling and its influence on tumor immunity:

  1. Regulation of Immune Cell Infiltration:
    • PPP1R14A has been shown to correlate with the levels of various infiltrating immune cells across multiple cancer types. Its expression is significantly associated with the abundance of immune cells such as B cells, CD4+ T cells, CD8+ T cells, macrophages, and dendritic cells. This suggests that PPP1R14A may play a role in modulating the immune landscape within tumors, impacting how immune cells infiltrate and respond to cancer cells [1].
  2. Relationship with Immune Checkpoint Molecules:
    • The expression of PPP1R14A is linked to immune checkpoint molecules (ICMs), which are critical for regulating immune responses and preventing excessive inflammation. In certain cancers, high levels of PPP1R14A expression have been associated with a negative relationship with ICMs, indicating that it might influence the effectiveness of immunotherapy by affecting how immune checkpoints regulate T cell activity [1].
  3. Impact on Tumor Microenvironment:
    • Studies have indicated that PPP1R14A expression can affect the tumor microenvironment by altering the balance of immune cell types present. For instance, in some cancers, high PPP1R14A levels were correlated with increased infiltration of specific immune cell types while showing a negative correlation with others, suggesting a complex role in shaping the immune response to tumors [1].
  4. Potential as a Prognostic Biomarker:
    • Given its association with immune cell infiltration and checkpoint regulation, PPP1R14A may serve as a prognostic biomarker in cancer. Its expression levels could help predict patient outcomes and responses to immunotherapy, particularly in tumors where immune evasion is a concern [1].
  5. Role in Cancer Progression:
    • By influencing both immune cell dynamics and signaling pathways involved in tumorigenesis, PPP1R14A may play a dual role in promoting cancer progression while also modulating the host’s immune response against tumors [2].

In summary, PPP1R14A is an important regulator of immune responses in the context of cancer, influencing immune cell infiltration, checkpoint regulation, and potentially serving as a prognostic biomarker for treatment outcomes. Its role in shaping the tumor microenvironment highlights its significance in both tumor biology and immunology.

TBX5

The immune function of the gene TBX5 (T-box 5) is primarily associated with its role in the development and regulation of immune cells, particularly in the context of T cell differentiation and function:

  1. Role in T Cell Development:
    • TBX5 is a member of the T-box family of transcription factors, which are crucial for various developmental processes, including the development of immune cells. It is involved in the differentiation of T cells, particularly influencing their maturation and functional capabilities.
  2. Influence on Th Cell Differentiation:
    • While TBX5 is not as extensively studied as other T-box genes like TBX21 (T-bet), it may still play a role in modulating the balance between different T helper (Th) cell subsets. For example, it could influence the differentiation of Th1 and Th2 cells, impacting the overall immune response to infections and allergens.
  3. Potential Role in Cardiac Immunity:
    • TBX5 has been implicated in cardiac development, but its expression in immune cells suggests a potential role in cardiac immunity. It may influence how immune cells interact with cardiac tissues, especially during inflammatory responses or in conditions like myocarditis.
  4. Regulation of Cytokine Production:
    • As a transcription factor, TBX5 may regulate genes involved in cytokine production, thereby influencing the inflammatory response. This regulation is essential for coordinating the immune response during infections or tissue damage.
  5. Impact on Autoimmunity:
    • Alterations in TBX5 expression or function could potentially contribute to autoimmune conditions by affecting T cell differentiation and function. Dysregulation of T cell responses can lead to inappropriate immune activation against self-antigens.
  6. Interplay with Other Immune Regulators:
    • TBX5 may interact with other transcription factors and signaling pathways that regulate immune responses, contributing to a complex network that governs T cell behavior and overall immunity.

In summary, TBX5 plays a significant role in regulating T cell development and function within the immune system. Its involvement in cytokine regulation and potential impact on autoimmunity highlight its importance in maintaining immune homeostasis and responding effectively to pathogens. Further research is needed to fully elucidate its specific roles and mechanisms within the immune context.

DDX52

The immune function of the gene DDX52 (DEAD-box helicase 52) is primarily associated with its regulatory role in innate immunity, particularly in response to viral infections:

  1. Regulation of Antiviral Responses:
    • DDX52 has been identified as a negative regulator of the antiviral innate immune response. It influences the production of type I interferons (IFNs), which are crucial for initiating antiviral defenses. Overexpression of DDX52 can inhibit IFN production, thereby facilitating viral replication and impairing the host’s ability to mount an effective immune response against viral pathogens [1][2].
  2. Interaction with Signaling Pathways:
    • DDX52 interacts with key components of the RLR (RIG-I-like receptor) signaling pathway, such as TBK1 (TANK-binding kinase 1). By promoting the degradation of TBK1, DDX52 disrupts the formation of the TBK1-TRAF3 complex, which is essential for activating downstream signaling that leads to IFN production. This action further dampens the antiviral response [2].
  3. Influence on Cytokine Production:
    • In addition to its effects on IFN production, DDX52 has been shown to regulate other cytokines involved in the immune response. For example, it can inhibit the expression of pro-inflammatory cytokines like IL-6, which are critical for coordinating immune responses during infections [1].
  4. Role in Viral Propagation:
    • By inhibiting key antiviral pathways and promoting viral replication, DDX52 plays a dual role in both supporting viral life cycles and modulating host immune responses. This makes it a target of interest in understanding viral pathogenesis and developing antiviral therapies [3].
  5. Potential as a Therapeutic Target:
    • Given its role as a negative regulator of innate immunity, targeting DDX52 may offer therapeutic avenues for enhancing antiviral responses in infected individuals or for developing strategies against viruses that exploit this pathway for replication [4].

In summary, DDX52 functions as a critical regulator of innate immunity by negatively influencing antiviral responses through its interactions with key signaling pathways and cytokine production. Its role in promoting viral propagation highlights its significance in both immunology and virology.

IQGAP1

The immune function of the gene IQGAP1 (IQ Motif Containing GTPase Activating Protein 1) is multifaceted and plays a critical role in regulating various immune cell functions through its involvement in signaling pathways and cytoskeletal dynamics:

  1. Regulation of Immune Cell Function:
    • IQGAP1 acts as a scaffolding protein that organizes signaling molecules within immune cells. It is involved in processes such as phagocytosis in macrophages and cell migration in neutrophils, facilitating effective immune responses to pathogens[1][3].
  2. Natural Killer (NK) Cell Activity:
    • IQGAP1 is essential for NK cell homeostasis and function. It helps regulate NK cell motility and their ability to produce inflammatory cytokines upon activation through natural killer receptors (NKRs). In the absence of IQGAP1, NK cells exhibit reduced motility and impaired antitumor immunity, indicating its crucial role in NK cell-mediated responses[1][3].
  3. T Cell Receptor Signaling:
    • In T cells, IQGAP1 negatively regulates T cell receptor (TCR) signaling and the dynamics of filamentous actin at the immunological synapse. This regulation can influence cytokine secretion, such as IL-2 and IFN-γ, highlighting its role in modulating T cell activation[3][4].
  4. Cytokine Production:
    • IQGAP1 has been shown to influence the production of type I interferons (IFNs) in response to cytosolic nucleic acids. Knockdown of IQGAP1 leads to increased IFN-β production, suggesting that it acts as a negative regulator of this pathway, thereby modulating the immune response to viral infections[4].
  5. Phagocytosis and Inflammatory Responses:
    • In macrophages, IQGAP1 facilitates phagocytosis and the secretion of pro-inflammatory cytokines like IL-1β. Its interaction with actin-nucleating proteins is crucial for forming phagocytic cups during engulfment processes[3][4].
  6. Interaction with Other Signaling Molecules:
    • IQGAP1 interacts with various proteins involved in immune signaling, including NLRC3, which also plays a role in regulating type I IFN responses. This interaction suggests a complex network where IQGAP1 may help fine-tune immune signaling pathways[4].

In summary, IQGAP1 is a critical regulator of immune functions through its roles in modulating NK cell activity, T cell signaling, phagocytosis, and cytokine production. Its ability to act as a scaffold for signaling molecules underscores its importance in maintaining effective immune responses and homeostasis within the immune system.

CCDC88C

The immune function of the gene CCDC88C (Coiled-Coil Domain Containing Protein 88C) is primarily associated with its roles in immune cell signaling, particularly in the context of T cell activation and dendritic cell (DC) function:

  1. Regulation of T Cell Activation:
    • CCDC88C is implicated in the activation and proliferation of CD4+ T cells. Its expression levels correlate with CD4+ T cell activation, suggesting that it plays a role in enhancing T cell responses during immune challenges, such as infections or tumors. This regulation is essential for effective adaptive immune responses.
  2. Influence on Dendritic Cell Function:
    • CCDC88C is critical for the migration and function of dendritic cells. Studies indicate that CCDC88C-deficient dendritic cells show impaired migration to draining lymph nodes upon inflammatory stimuli (e.g., LPS). This defect leads to reduced recruitment and activation of antigen-specific T cells, highlighting CCDC88C’s role in coordinating the immune response through DCs.
  3. Impact on Cytokine Production:
    • The absence of CCDC88C affects the production of pro-inflammatory cytokines in response to various stimuli. This suggests that CCDC88C is involved in regulating the inflammatory response, which is crucial for orchestrating immune reactions.
  4. Association with Inflammatory Diseases:
    • Variants in the CCDC88C gene have been associated with susceptibility to several inflammatory and autoimmune diseases in humans. This connection underscores its importance in maintaining immune homeostasis and preventing excessive inflammation.
  5. Role in Immune Cell Migration:
    • CCDC88C facilitates the motility of immune cells, particularly dendritic cells, which is vital for their ability to survey tissues and present antigens to T cells. Impaired migration due to CCDC88C deficiency can lead to diminished immune surveillance and responses.
  6. Potential Therapeutic Target:
    • Given its critical role in regulating T cell and dendritic cell functions, targeting CCDC88C may offer therapeutic avenues for enhancing immune responses in vaccines or improving immunotherapy outcomes in cancer treatment.

In summary, CCDC88C plays a significant role in regulating T cell activation and dendritic cell function, influencing cytokine production and immune cell migration. Its involvement in inflammatory diseases highlights its importance in maintaining immune balance and responding effectively to pathogens.

CHMP4C

The immune function of the gene CHMP4C (Charged Multivesicular Body Protein 4C) is primarily associated with its role in the Endosomal Sorting Complex Required for Transport (ESCRT) pathway, which is crucial for various cellular processes, including immune responses:

  1. Role in Viral Budding:
    • CHMP4C is a key component of the ESCRT-III complex, which is involved in the budding and release of enveloped viruses, including HIV and herpes simplex virus (HSV). By facilitating the final stages of viral budding, CHMP4C plays a critical role in controlling viral replication and dissemination, thereby influencing the host’s immune response to viral infections [1][2].
  2. Regulation of Cytokine Secretion:
    • The ESCRT machinery, including CHMP4C, is also involved in the secretion of cytokines and other signaling molecules from immune cells. This regulation is essential for coordinating immune responses, as cytokines play a pivotal role in mediating communication between immune cells and orchestrating inflammatory responses.
  3. Antigen Presentation:
    • CHMP4C may influence the processing and presentation of antigens by regulating the trafficking of major histocompatibility complex (MHC) molecules. Proper functioning of the ESCRT pathway is crucial for maintaining the integrity of antigen presentation processes, which are vital for T cell activation and adaptive immunity [4].
  4. Innate Immune Responses:
    • CHMP4C has been implicated in innate immune signaling pathways, particularly those involving pattern recognition receptors (PRRs). By participating in the endosomal trafficking of these receptors, CHMP4C can modulate the activation of downstream signaling cascades that lead to the production of type I interferons and other pro-inflammatory cytokines [1].
  5. Impact on Immune Cell Dynamics:
    • Beyond its roles in viral budding and cytokine secretion, CHMP4C contributes to the overall dynamics of immune cells by regulating membrane remodeling processes that are essential for cell migration and interaction with other immune cells.
  6. Potential Therapeutic Target:
    • Given its involvement in viral pathogenesis and immune regulation, targeting CHMP4C or related ESCRT components may offer therapeutic strategies for enhancing antiviral immunity or modulating inflammatory responses in various diseases.

In summary, CHMP4C is a critical player in the ESCRT pathway with significant implications for viral budding, cytokine secretion, antigen presentation, and overall immune cell function. Its roles underscore its importance in both innate and adaptive immunity, particularly in response to viral infections.

ZNF217

The immune function of the gene ZNF217 (Zinc Finger Protein 217) is primarily associated with its roles in regulating immune responses, particularly in the context of inflammation and cancer:

  1. Regulation of Immune Cell Function:
    • ZNF217 has been implicated in modulating the function of various immune cells, including T cells and macrophages. It can influence the differentiation and activation of these cells, thereby impacting overall immune responses.
  2. Influence on Inflammatory Responses:
    • ZNF217 is involved in the regulation of inflammatory cytokines. Its expression can affect the production of pro-inflammatory cytokines, which are crucial for coordinating immune responses during infections or tissue damage. This suggests that ZNF217 may play a role in maintaining the balance between pro-inflammatory and anti-inflammatory signals.
  3. Role in Cancer Immunology:
    • ZNF217 has been associated with cancer progression and immune evasion. It can promote tumor cell survival and proliferation while suppressing anti-tumor immune responses. By influencing the expression of genes involved in immune regulation, ZNF217 may help tumors escape detection and destruction by the immune system.
  4. Potential as a Therapeutic Target:
    • Given its involvement in both inflammation and cancer, ZNF217 may represent a potential therapeutic target for enhancing anti-tumor immunity or modulating inflammatory diseases. Targeting ZNF217 could help restore effective immune responses against tumors or reduce excessive inflammation in autoimmune conditions.
  5. Interplay with Other Transcription Factors:
    • ZNF217 may interact with other transcription factors and signaling pathways that regulate immune responses, contributing to a complex network that governs how immune cells respond to various stimuli.

In summary, ZNF217 plays a significant role in regulating immune functions by influencing the activation and differentiation of immune cells, modulating inflammatory responses, and impacting tumor immunity. Its functions highlight its importance in maintaining immune homeostasis and responding effectively to pathological conditions. Further research into ZNF217 could provide insights into its potential as a target for therapeutic interventions in cancer and inflammatory diseases.

TXN

The immune function of the gene TXN (Thioredoxin) is primarily associated with its role in redox regulation, which is crucial for maintaining cellular homeostasis and modulating immune responses:

  1. Redox Regulation:
    • TXN functions as an antioxidant by catalyzing the reduction of disulfide bonds in proteins, thereby protecting cells from oxidative stress. This redox activity is vital for the proper functioning of immune cells, as oxidative stress can impair their function and viability.
  2. Modulation of Immune Responses:
    • TXN has been shown to influence the activation and proliferation of various immune cells, including T cells and macrophages. By regulating the redox state within these cells, TXN can modulate their responses to cytokines and other signaling molecules, affecting overall immune function.
  3. Cytokine Production:
    • TXN plays a role in the production of cytokines, which are critical for communication between immune cells. For instance, it can enhance the secretion of pro-inflammatory cytokines in response to pathogens or inflammatory stimuli, thereby promoting an effective immune response.
  4. Regulation of Inflammation:
    • By influencing the balance between oxidative and reductive states, TXN can help regulate inflammatory processes. Its activity is essential for preventing excessive inflammation that could lead to tissue damage and chronic inflammatory diseases.
  5. Role in Cellular Senescence and Inflammaging:
    • TXN is involved in cellular senescence and the senescence-associated secretory phenotype (SASP), which contributes to chronic inflammation associated with aging (inflammaging). This suggests that TXN may play a dual role in both promoting immune responses and contributing to age-related inflammation.
  6. Implications in Disease:
    • Dysregulation of TXN has been linked to various diseases, including autoimmune disorders and cancer. Its role in modulating oxidative stress and inflammatory responses makes it a potential target for therapeutic interventions aimed at restoring normal immune function.

In summary, TXN is a critical regulator of immune function through its roles in redox regulation, modulation of cytokine production, and control of inflammatory responses. Its importance in maintaining cellular homeostasis highlights its significance in both innate and adaptive immunity.

TBX1

The immune function of the gene TBX1 (T-box 1) is primarily associated with its critical roles in immune system development and function, particularly in the context of T cell maturation and the regulation of immune responses:

  1. T Cell Development:
    • TBX1 is essential for the proper development of T cells in the thymus. It plays a pivotal role in the differentiation of thymocytes into functional T cells, influencing their maturation and selection processes. This is crucial for establishing a competent adaptive immune response.
  2. Regulation of Thymic Function:
    • TBX1 is involved in the development of thymic epithelial cells, which are essential for T cell maturation. Proper functioning of TBX1 ensures that these cells can support the positive and negative selection processes that are vital for producing self-tolerant T cells.
  3. Influence on Immune Responses:
    • Beyond T cell development, TBX1 has been implicated in regulating various aspects of immune responses. It can influence the expression of cytokines and other signaling molecules that modulate immune activation and inflammation.
  4. Role in Congenital Disorders:
    • Mutations or deletions affecting TBX1 are associated with DiGeorge syndrome, a condition that results in immunodeficiency due to thymic hypoplasia. This highlights TBX1’s critical role in immune system integrity and function.
  5. Potential Impact on Autoimmunity and Inflammation:
    • Given its regulatory roles, TBX1 may also be involved in autoimmune processes and inflammatory responses. Dysregulation of TBX1 expression can lead to aberrant immune activation or tolerance breakdown.
  6. Interactions with Other Transcription Factors:
    • TBX1 interacts with other transcription factors involved in T cell differentiation and function, contributing to a complex network that governs immune cell behavior.

In summary, TBX1 is a vital transcription factor that plays significant roles in T cell development, thymic function, and the regulation of immune responses. Its importance is underscored by its involvement in congenital immunodeficiencies and potential implications in autoimmune diseases.

WNT2

The immune function of the gene WNT2 (Wnt Family Member 2) is primarily associated with its role in modulating immune responses, particularly through the Wnt signaling pathway. Here are some key aspects of its immune functions:

  1. Modulation of Immune Cell Differentiation:
    • WNT2 is involved in the differentiation and activation of various immune cells, including T cells and dendritic cells. It plays a role in promoting T cell lymphopoiesis, which is essential for the development of a robust adaptive immune response.
  2. Regulation of Cytokine Production:
    • WNT2 influences the production of cytokines that are critical for orchestrating immune responses. For instance, it can enhance the secretion of pro-inflammatory cytokines, thereby contributing to the inflammatory response during infections.
  3. Involvement in Antigen Presentation:
    • The Wnt signaling pathway, including WNT2, has been shown to affect the function of antigen-presenting cells (APCs). This includes enhancing their ability to present antigens to T cells, which is crucial for initiating adaptive immunity.
  4. Impact on Tumor Immunology:
    • WNT2 has been implicated in cancer immunology, where it can contribute to tumor immune evasion. Activation of Wnt signaling in tumor cells can inhibit the recruitment and function of cytotoxic T lymphocytes (CTLs), thereby allowing tumors to escape immune surveillance.
  5. Role in Inflammatory Diseases:
    • Aberrant Wnt signaling, including that mediated by WNT2, has been linked to various inflammatory diseases. Dysregulation of this pathway can lead to excessive inflammation or altered immune responses, contributing to conditions such as rheumatoid arthritis or inflammatory bowel disease.
  6. Cross-Talk with Other Signaling Pathways:
    • WNT2 interacts with other signaling pathways that regulate immune responses, highlighting its role in a complex network that governs how immune cells respond to various stimuli.

In summary, WNT2 plays a significant role in regulating immune functions through its involvement in T cell differentiation, cytokine production, antigen presentation, and modulation of tumor immunity. Its influence on inflammatory processes further underscores its importance in maintaining immune homeostasis and responding effectively to pathogens and tumors.

RPS6KL1

The immune function of the gene RPS6KL1 (Ribosomal Protein S6 Kinase-Like 1) is primarily associated with its role in regulating immune responses and cell signaling, particularly in the context of T cell activation and inflammation:

  1. Regulation of T Cell Activation:
    • RPS6KL1 is involved in the signaling pathways that control T cell activation and proliferation. It may influence the translation of mRNAs that encode proteins essential for T cell responses, thereby impacting the overall effectiveness of adaptive immunity.
  2. Cytokine Production:
    • The gene has been implicated in the regulation of cytokine production in immune cells. By modulating the translation and expression of cytokines, RPS6KL1 can affect inflammatory responses and the communication between different immune cell types.
  3. Impact on Inflammatory Responses:
    • RPS6KL1 may play a role in the inflammatory response by regulating the production of pro-inflammatory cytokines. This is crucial for coordinating immune responses during infections or tissue injury.
  4. Potential Role in Autoimmune Diseases:
    • Dysregulation of RPS6KL1 could contribute to autoimmune conditions by affecting T cell activation and leading to inappropriate immune responses against self-antigens.
  5. Cellular Proliferation and Survival:
    • The gene is involved in pathways that regulate cellular proliferation and survival, which are critical for maintaining healthy immune cell populations and ensuring effective immune responses.
  6. Interactions with Other Signaling Pathways:
    • RPS6KL1 interacts with various signaling pathways that govern immune cell function, including those related to mTOR (mechanistic target of rapamycin), which is vital for nutrient sensing and cellular growth.

In summary, RPS6KL1 plays a significant role in regulating T cell activation, cytokine production, and inflammatory responses within the immune system. Its functions highlight its importance in maintaining immune homeostasis and responding effectively to pathogens. Further research may provide deeper insights into its specific mechanisms and potential therapeutic implications in immune-related diseases.

MLPH

The immune function of the gene MLPH (Melanophilin) is primarily associated with its role in regulating immune cell dynamics and responses, particularly in the context of macrophage function and inflammation:

  1. Role in Macrophage Function:
    • MLPH is involved in the regulation of macrophage polarization and activation. It plays a role in modulating the transition between pro-inflammatory (M1) and anti-inflammatory (M2) macrophage states. This is crucial for orchestrating effective immune responses during infections and tissue repair.
  2. Influence on Cytokine Production:
    • MLPH has been implicated in the regulation of cytokine production in macrophages. By influencing the expression of various cytokines, it helps coordinate the inflammatory response, impacting how effectively the immune system can respond to pathogens.
  3. Impact on Immune Cell Migration:
    • MLPH is known to play a role in cytoskeletal dynamics, which are essential for the migration of immune cells to sites of infection or inflammation. This function is critical for ensuring that immune cells can effectively reach and respond to areas where they are needed.
  4. Potential Role in Inflammatory Diseases:
    • Dysregulation of MLPH may contribute to chronic inflammatory conditions by affecting macrophage activation and cytokine production. This could lead to an imbalance in pro-inflammatory and anti-inflammatory signals, perpetuating inflammation.
  5. Interaction with Other Signaling Pathways:
    • MLPH may interact with various signaling pathways that regulate immune responses, contributing to a complex network that governs immune cell behavior and function.

In summary, MLPH plays a significant role in regulating macrophage function, cytokine production, and immune cell migration. Its involvement in these processes underscores its importance in maintaining effective immune responses and managing inflammation. Further research could elucidate its specific mechanisms and potential therapeutic implications in inflammatory diseases.

DMRTA1

The immune function of the gene DMRTA1 (Doublesex and Mab-3 Related Transcription Factor A1) is not extensively characterized in the literature, but some insights can be inferred based on its roles in cellular processes that may influence immune responses:

  1. Transcriptional Regulation:
    • DMRTA1 is a transcription factor that may play a role in regulating gene expression related to immune functions. By influencing the transcription of specific genes, DMRTA1 could impact the differentiation and activation of immune cells.
  2. Potential Role in T Cell Development:
    • Although specific studies on DMRTA1’s role in T cell development are limited, transcription factors in the same family often have critical functions in cell fate determination and differentiation. This suggests that DMRTA1 may be involved in T cell maturation or function within the thymus.
  3. Influence on Inflammatory Responses:
    • DMRTA1 could potentially impact inflammatory responses by regulating cytokine production or influencing the activation states of immune cells. This would be important for coordinating effective immune responses during infections or tissue damage.
  4. Association with Immune Disorders:
    • While direct associations with specific immune disorders have not been well-documented, alterations in transcription factors like DMRTA1 can contribute to dysregulated immune responses, which may lead to autoimmune diseases or chronic inflammation.
  5. Research Gaps:
    • More research is needed to elucidate the specific mechanisms by which DMRTA1 influences immune functions. Functional studies would help clarify its role in various immune contexts, including its potential interactions with other signaling pathways.

In summary, while the specific immune functions of DMRTA1 are not well-defined, its role as a transcription factor suggests it may influence T cell development, cytokine production, and overall immune responses. Further research is necessary to fully understand its contributions to immunity and potential implications in immune-related diseases.

FBXO38

The immune function of the gene FBXO38 (F-box protein 38) is primarily associated with its role in regulating immune responses through the ubiquitin-proteasome system. Here are the key aspects of its immune functions:

  1. Ubiquitination and Protein Degradation:
    • FBXO38 is part of the F-box protein family, which functions as substrate recognition components of E3 ubiquitin ligases. It plays a critical role in tagging specific proteins for degradation, thereby regulating the levels of various signaling molecules involved in immune responses.
  2. Regulation of Cytokine Production:
    • By influencing the degradation of proteins that regulate cytokine signaling, FBXO38 can modulate the production of pro-inflammatory cytokines. This regulation is crucial for maintaining balanced immune responses and preventing excessive inflammation.
  3. Impact on Immune Cell Activation:
    • FBXO38 may influence the activation and differentiation of immune cells, including T cells and macrophages. Its role in protein turnover can affect how these cells respond to stimuli and their overall functionality during immune challenges.
  4. Role in Inflammatory Diseases:
    • Dysregulation of FBXO38 has been implicated in various inflammatory diseases. By affecting the stability and activity of key regulatory proteins, it may contribute to pathological conditions characterized by chronic inflammation.
  5. Potential Therapeutic Target:
    • Given its involvement in regulating immune responses, FBXO38 may represent a potential therapeutic target for modulating inflammation or enhancing immune responses in various diseases, including autoimmune disorders and cancer.
  6. Interplay with Other Immune Regulators:
    • FBXO38 interacts with other proteins involved in immune signaling pathways, contributing to a complex network that governs immune cell behavior and function.

In summary, FBXO38 plays a significant role in regulating immune functions through its involvement in protein ubiquitination and degradation, impacting cytokine production, immune cell activation, and inflammatory responses. Further research could elucidate its specific mechanisms and potential therapeutic implications in immune-related diseases.

WIPI1

The immune function of the gene WIPI1 (WD Repeat and Phosphoinositide Interacting Protein 1) is primarily linked to its role in autophagy and immune responses:

  1. Involvement in Autophagy:
    • WIPI1 is a key regulator of autophagy, a cellular process that degrades and recycles cellular components. It plays a crucial role in the formation of autophagosomes, which are essential for the degradation of pathogens and damaged organelles within immune cells. This process is vital for maintaining cellular homeostasis and responding to infections.
  2. Regulation of Immune Responses:
    • By facilitating autophagy, WIPI1 helps modulate immune responses. Autophagy is involved in the presentation of antigens to T cells, enhancing the adaptive immune response. This function is critical for effective pathogen clearance and the activation of immune cells.
  3. Role in Inflammation:
    • WIPI1 may also influence inflammatory responses. Autophagy can regulate the secretion of pro-inflammatory cytokines, thereby impacting inflammation levels during immune responses to infections or tissue damage.
  4. Interaction with Phosphoinositides:
    • WIPI1 binds to phosphoinositides, which are important for membrane trafficking processes in cells. This interaction is crucial for recruiting other autophagy-related proteins to sites of autophagosome formation, further supporting its role in immune cell function.
  5. Implications in Disease:
    • Dysregulation of WIPI1 and autophagy has been linked to various diseases, including infections and autoimmune disorders. Proper functioning of WIPI1 is essential for effective immune responses, and its dysfunction may contribute to impaired immunity.
  6. Potential Therapeutic Target:
    • Given its central role in autophagy and immune regulation, WIPI1 could be a potential therapeutic target for enhancing immune responses or modulating inflammation in various diseases.

In summary, WIPI1 plays a significant role in regulating autophagy and modulating immune responses through its involvement in antigen presentation and inflammatory regulation. Its functions highlight its importance in maintaining effective immunity and cellular homeostasis.

OSBPL5

The immune function of the gene OSBPL5 (Oxysterol-Binding Protein-Like 5) is increasingly recognized for its involvement in immune responses, particularly in the context of cancer and inflammation. Here are the key aspects of its immune functions based on recent findings:

  1. Regulation of Immune Cell Infiltration:
    • OSBPL5 expression has been correlated with the infiltration of various immune cell types within the tumor microenvironment. For instance, studies have shown that higher levels of OSBPL5 are associated with increased infiltration of CD8+ T cells and macrophages, suggesting a role in promoting an active immune environment in tumors like kidney renal clear cell carcinoma (KIRC) [1].
  2. Influence on Cytokine Production:
    • The expression of OSBPL5 may impact cytokine signaling pathways. It has been linked to the regulation of pro-inflammatory cytokines, which are crucial for coordinating immune responses during infections and in tumor contexts. This suggests that OSBPL5 could modulate inflammatory responses by affecting cytokine production.
  3. Potential Biomarker for Immune Responses:
    • Given its association with immune cell infiltration and cytokine production, OSBPL5 may serve as a potential biomarker for assessing immune responses in various cancers. Its expression levels could help predict patient outcomes and responses to immunotherapy [1][2].
  4. Interaction with Immune Checkpoints:
    • There is evidence that OSBPL5 interacts with immune checkpoint molecules such as PD-L1, which plays a critical role in tumor immune evasion. The expression of OSBPL5 has been shown to correlate with PD-L1 levels, indicating its potential role in regulating T cell activity and immune suppression in the tumor microenvironment [1].
  5. Role in Lipid Metabolism and Immune Function:
    • As a member of the oxysterol-binding protein-like family, OSBPL5 is involved in lipid transport and metabolism, which are essential for maintaining cellular functions and modulating immune responses. Lipid metabolism can influence the activation and differentiation of immune cells, further linking OSBPL5 to immune regulation [2][3].
  6. Implications in Cancer Immunology:
    • The upregulation of OSBPL5 in tumors suggests it may play a role in tumor progression and immune evasion mechanisms. Its involvement in promoting an immunosuppressive environment highlights its significance in cancer immunology [1][4].

In summary, OSBPL5 plays a significant role in regulating immune functions through its influence on immune cell infiltration, cytokine production, interactions with immune checkpoints, and lipid metabolism. Its potential as a biomarker for cancer prognosis and therapy underscores its importance in understanding tumor immunity and developing targeted immunotherapies.

NUCKS1

The immune function of the gene NUCKS1 (Nuclear Casein Kinase and Cyclin-Dependent Kinase Substrate 1) is associated with several important roles in immune responses, particularly in inflammation and cytokine regulation:

  1. Regulation of Inflammatory Immune Responses:
    • NUCKS1 is involved in modulating inflammatory responses. Studies have shown that inhibition of NUCKS1 can affect cytokine modulation, facilitating recovery in corneal injuries by decreasing the expression of angiogenic factors like vascular endothelial growth factor (VEGF) while increasing anti-angiogenic factors such as pigment epithelium-derived factor (PEDF) [2][3].
  2. NF-κB Signaling Pathway:
    • NUCKS1 plays a critical role in the NF-κB signaling pathway, which is essential for the expression of various pro-inflammatory cytokines. For instance, following lipopolysaccharide (LPS) stimulation, NUCKS1 knockout cells exhibited reduced phosphorylation of IκB and lower levels of interleukins (including IL-6), IP10, and tumor necrosis factor-alpha (TNF-α). This indicates that NUCKS1 is important for the activation of NF-κB and subsequent cytokine expression [2][3].
  3. DNA Damage Response:
    • Beyond its role in inflammation, NUCKS1 is involved in the DNA damage response and maintenance of genomic stability. This function can indirectly influence immune responses by ensuring that immune cells can effectively respond to stressors and maintain their integrity during inflammatory processes [3].
  4. Cytokine Modulation:
    • NUCKS1 has been linked to the modulation of various cytokines, affecting both pro-inflammatory and anti-inflammatory pathways. Its ability to regulate these pathways makes it a significant player in balancing immune responses during infections and inflammatory conditions [2][3].
  5. Potential Role in Cancer Immunology:
    • Elevated levels of NUCKS1 have been associated with increased tumor invasiveness and may play a role in cancer progression by influencing immune evasion mechanisms. This suggests that NUCKS1 could affect how tumors interact with the immune system [3].

In summary, NUCKS1 plays a multifaceted role in immune function by regulating inflammatory responses through NF-κB signaling, modulating cytokine production, and maintaining genomic stability in immune cells. Its involvement in both inflammation and cancer highlights its significance in understanding immune regulation and potential therapeutic targets.

RFC5

The immune function of the gene RFC5 (Replication Factor C Subunit 5) is primarily associated with its role in DNA replication and repair, which has significant implications for immune responses:

  1. Role in DNA Replication and Repair:
    • RFC5 is a component of the Replication Factor C (RFC) complex, which is essential for loading the sliding clamp protein PCNA (Proliferating Cell Nuclear Antigen) onto DNA during replication. This function is crucial for maintaining genomic stability in immune cells, particularly during the rapid proliferation that occurs during immune responses.
  2. Influence on Immune Cell Proliferation:
    • By facilitating DNA replication, RFC5 plays a critical role in the proliferation of immune cells, such as T and B lymphocytes. Proper cell division is essential for generating sufficient numbers of these cells to mount an effective adaptive immune response.
  3. Regulation of Immune Responses:
    • RFC5 may also influence the expression of genes involved in immune signaling pathways. Its role in DNA repair processes ensures that immune cells can respond effectively to stressors, including infections and inflammation.
  4. Association with Immune Disorders:
    • Dysregulation of RFC5 expression has been linked to various cancers and may affect how immune cells function within the tumor microenvironment. Increased expression of RFC family members, including RFC5, has been associated with poor prognosis in certain cancers, potentially due to their impact on immune cell infiltration and activity.
  5. Impact on Immune Cell Infiltration:
    • Studies have indicated that higher levels of RFC expression correlate negatively with the infiltration of CD4+ T cells and macrophages in tumor settings. This suggests that RFC5 may play a role in modulating the immune landscape within tumors, affecting anti-tumor immunity.
  6. Potential Therapeutic Target:
    • Given its involvement in DNA replication and repair, targeting RFC5 or its associated pathways may offer therapeutic strategies for enhancing immune responses or improving outcomes in cancer immunotherapy.

In summary, RFC5 plays a significant role in regulating DNA replication and repair processes that are crucial for immune cell proliferation and function. Its influence on immune responses and potential implications in cancer highlight its importance in maintaining effective immunity and cellular integrity.

MBNL1

The immune function of the gene MBNL1 (Muscleblind-like splicing regulator 1) is primarily associated with its role in alternative RNA splicing, particularly in the context of T cell development and function:

  1. Regulation of Thymocyte Development:
    • MBNL1 is essential for normal thymic development, which is critical for T lymphocyte maturation. It regulates RNA processing during thymocyte development, ensuring proper expression of genes involved in T cell differentiation and selection. Loss of MBNL1 leads to dysregulated gene expression and RNA misprocessing in the thymus, which can adversely affect T cell development and function [3][4].
  2. Impact on Immune Cell Function:
    • By influencing alternative splicing, MBNL1 affects the expression of various proteins that are crucial for immune responses. This includes proteins involved in T cell receptor (TCR) signaling, which is vital for T cell activation and responses to pathogens.
  3. Cytokine Production:
    • MBNL1 may play a role in regulating cytokine production by modulating the splicing of mRNAs that encode cytokines or their receptors. This regulation is important for coordinating immune responses during infections and inflammation.
  4. Association with Immune Disorders:
    • Dysregulation of MBNL1 has been implicated in various diseases, including certain leukemias where it is overexpressed. In these contexts, MBNL1 can influence the splicing of genes involved in cancer progression, potentially affecting the tumor microenvironment and immune evasion mechanisms [4].
  5. Potential as a Therapeutic Target:
    • Given its role in regulating immune cell development and function, MBNL1 could be a potential therapeutic target for enhancing immune responses or correcting dysregulated splicing events in immune-related diseases.

In summary, MBNL1 plays a significant role in regulating T cell development through its involvement in alternative RNA splicing. Its influence on immune cell function and potential implications in immune disorders highlight its importance in maintaining effective immune responses. Further research could elucidate its specific mechanisms and therapeutic potential in various contexts.

RP11-77H9.1

The immune function of the gene RP11-77H9.1 (also known as RP11-770J1.4) has been identified in the context of its regulatory roles in immune responses, particularly in relation to gliomas:

  1. Regulation of Immune Responses:
    • RP11-77H9.1 is involved in regulating the expression of genes associated with immune responses, specifically through its interaction with the cytosolic DNA sensing pathway. This pathway is crucial for detecting intracellular DNA and initiating immune responses against infections and tumors.
  2. Interaction with the cGAS-STING Pathway:
    • The long non-coding RNA (lncRNA) RP11-77H9.1 has been shown to regulate the expression of CTXN1 (Cortexin 1) by sponging hsa-miR-124-3p. Downregulation of RP11-77H9.1 leads to increased activation of the cGAS-STING pathway, which is vital for triggering immune responses, particularly the production of type I interferons that enhance anti-tumor immunity.
  3. Impact on Tumor Microenvironment:
    • In glioma models, decreased expression of RP11-77H9.1 correlates with increased infiltration of CD8+ T cells, which are essential for effective anti-tumor immunity. This suggests that RP11-77H9.1 may play a role in modulating the tumor microenvironment by influencing immune cell infiltration and activity.
  4. Potential as a Therapeutic Target:
    • The findings indicate that targeting RP11-77H9.1 could enhance immune responses in gliomas, making it a potential therapeutic target for improving outcomes in patients with this type of cancer.
  5. Correlation with Prognosis:
    • Survival analyses have demonstrated a close correlation between RP11-77H9.1 expression and glioma prognosis, suggesting that it may serve as a biomarker for assessing immune-related features in tumors and predicting patient outcomes.

In summary, RP11-77H9.1 functions as an important regulator of immune responses through its involvement in the cGAS-STING pathway and its impact on T cell infiltration in gliomas. Its role highlights its potential significance in cancer immunotherapy and as a prognostic marker in tumor biology.

UQCC

The immune function of the gene UQCC (Ubiquinone-Cytochrome c Reductase Core Component) is primarily associated with its role in mitochondrial function and cellular metabolism, which are critical for effective immune responses:

  1. Mitochondrial Function and Energy Production:
    • UQCC is involved in the mitochondrial respiratory chain, specifically in the complex III assembly, which is essential for ATP production. Adequate energy supply is crucial for the activation and proliferation of immune cells, particularly during immune responses to infections.
  2. Regulation of Reactive Oxygen Species (ROS):
    • By participating in mitochondrial electron transport, UQCC helps regulate the production of reactive oxygen species (ROS). ROS play a dual role in the immune system; they can act as signaling molecules that enhance immune responses but can also contribute to tissue damage if produced excessively. Proper regulation of ROS levels is essential for maintaining a balanced immune response.
  3. Influence on Immune Cell Activation:
    • The activity of UQCC may impact the activation and function of various immune cells, including T cells and macrophages. Effective mitochondrial function is vital for these cells to respond adequately to pathogens and inflammatory signals.
  4. Potential Role in Inflammation:
    • UQCC may influence inflammatory processes by affecting the metabolic state of immune cells. Changes in metabolism can alter cytokine production and cell signaling pathways, impacting overall inflammatory responses.
  5. Association with Disease:
    • Dysregulation of UQCC and mitochondrial function has been linked to various diseases, including autoimmune disorders and cancer. Impaired mitochondrial function can lead to altered immune responses, contributing to disease pathogenesis.
  6. Research Gaps:
    • While the specific immune functions of UQCC are not fully characterized, further research could elucidate its precise roles in immune regulation and potential therapeutic implications in immune-related diseases.

In summary, UQCC plays a significant role in mitochondrial function and energy production, which are essential for effective immune responses. Its influence on ROS regulation and potential impact on inflammation highlight its importance in maintaining immune homeostasis. Further studies are needed to explore its specific mechanisms and implications in various diseases.
